<div id="review_1384694778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1384694778" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22129064-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603829793p2/22129064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1384694778?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/22129064-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22129064-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22129064-laura?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22129064-laura?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22129064-laura?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22129064-laura?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1384694778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer41393425364122304">This is such a lovely, sweet book written in verse. It hardly feels like verse though because it reads so smoothly. You can gather and infer so much from the way the lines are formatted! For that reason, I really liked it and would definitely reread it! Well, that and other reasons!<br/><br/>For one thing, I love how the sparrow is incorporated into Elaine's journey. That's what this book is really about: Elaine's journey to find herself and where she belongs in the world. She has an idea at the beginning</span>
  <span id="freeText41393425364122304" style="display:none">This is such a lovely, sweet book written in verse. It hardly feels like verse though because it reads so smoothly. You can gather and infer so much from the way the lines are formatted! For that reason, I really liked it and would definitely reread it! Well, that and other reasons!<br /><br />For one thing, I love how the sparrow is incorporated into Elaine's journey. That's what this book is really about: Elaine's journey to find herself and where she belongs in the world. She has an idea at the beginning of the book but it isn't clear and she isn't satisfied with her life. She thinks she wants certain things only to find out that they aren't for her. The sparrow represents her spirit and how, at the beginning, it is trapped within her and only at the end is it set free.<br /><br />The story is set in the time of Arthur and Lancelot and the Round Table which was really cool to read about. However, be prepared that the story centers around Elaine and her personal internal struggles rather than the war or anything else going on at that time. To that end, I really liked how the author incorporated the Round Table and put her personal spin on the story.<br /><br />The Final Verdict:<br />All in all, this is such a sweet little book about a girl's struggle to find herself and where she belongs in the world. It's not really anything deep but not entirely fluffy either.<br />4 stars<br /><br /><br />Quotes:<br />“I live, yet” <br /><br /><br />“Still, I look down, and the grass is so green, I cannot understand how it does not wither and die with sorrow."<br /><br /><br />“Love is a tempestuous mistress.<br />And none of us shall ever master her.” <br /><br /><br />“It should begin with friendship, I think. Suddenly I cannot look at him.<br />It should begin with friendship and truly knowing who a person is, knowing his flaws and hopes and strengths and fears, knowing all of it. And admiring and caring for- loving the person because of all of those things...<br />I know that now.” <br /><br /><br />“My sparrow, she flickers and wakes and sings and sings. ” </span>
  <a data-text-id="41393425364122304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_37532062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37532062" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/398239-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448427826p2/398239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37532062?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/398239-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/398239-michelle?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/398239-michelle?shelf=fairy-folk-tales">fairy-folk-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/398239-michelle?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/398239-michelle?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37532062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6345672395036443210">I'll admit it first thing: I was a King Arthur groupie. Summers were spent at Renaissance festivals, and one year my best friend and I even made medieval dresses for ourselves - and it wasn't even close to Halloween. So coming into this lovely, lovely book which retells the story of Elaine, the Lady of Shalott, I was more than excited. Then I opened the book and saw it was all in verse and I sort of did a little dance around the house. Okay, so it was a big happy dance. <br/><br/>In this revised version o</span>
  <span id="freeText6345672395036443210" style="display:none">I'll admit it first thing: I was a King Arthur groupie. Summers were spent at Renaissance festivals, and one year my best friend and I even made medieval dresses for ourselves - and it wasn't even close to Halloween. So coming into this lovely, lovely book which retells the story of Elaine, the Lady of Shalott, I was more than excited. Then I opened the book and saw it was all in verse and I sort of did a little dance around the house. Okay, so it was a big happy dance. <br /><br />In this revised version of The Lady of Shaott, Elaine along with her brothers and father live in the soldiers camp under the direction of Arthur. She has become friend, sister and healer to the men but her only wish is that she could have more female friends. As war progresses, Elaine gets her wish when Lancelot, the love of her life, brings back Gwynivere to be Arthur's bride. But Lancelot is obviously in love with Gwyn and can only see Elaine as a young girl. To make matters worse, Gwyn is utterly beautiful and completely mean and nasty to Elaine. Which I thought was a totally delicious change.<br /><br />Sandell may not have stayed completely true to Tennyson's original poem about Elaine, but this version was more filled with hope for the future. The cadence and smooth flow of events competely had me sucked in from the very beginning. Here's one of my favorite passages: <br /><br />"The warriors gather, but I am not welcome./ Or so Lavaian tells me, hurling / the words like rocks over his shoulder. / Stay here. The meeting is no place for a girl. / Leaving me here, alone, / to wait and wonder. / What will become of us?"<br /><br />Just so dang great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6345672395036443210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('97VmtmDFJVSIMUYSbY07jolt6VK1tAEtUcyUopoEvkChPIUSYVr7KPuaM4UL7vbSEfBOPabkljGMlgoNHiFJuw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DuxxjM592GhZK1cUfOFSC7IVTjk/4bM2qond8IjFOMlYZZIoz+IGFCqAIoMagp9XKojpViyxJCp300NfDODPMg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17425941850821705462">I was born and raised in Wilmington, Delaware, where I'm told that I was forever buried in books. I began scribbling my own short stories in a spiral bound notebook when I was six. Books and writing were--and still are--a haven for me, and I count myself so lucky that I have a chance to share my stories with others. I currently live and work in New York City where, when I'm not writing, I'm riding</span>
  <span id="freeText17425941850821705462" style="display:none">I was born and raised in Wilmington, Delaware, where I'm told that I was forever buried in books. I began scribbling my own short stories in a spiral bound notebook when I was six. Books and writing were--and still are--a haven for me, and I count myself so lucky that I have a chance to share my stories with others. I currently live and work in New York City where, when I'm not writing, I'm riding my bike, taking a sculpting class, or playing with my dog, Molly. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17425941850821705462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/553929-song-of-the-sparrow">Quotes from Song of the Sparrow</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;It should begin with friendship, I think. Suddenly I cannot look at him.<br />It should begin with friendship and truly knowing who a person is, knowing his flaws and hopes and strengths and fears, knowing all of it. And admiring and caring for- loving the person because of all of those things...<br />I know that now.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/123737-it-should-begin-with-friendship-i-think-suddenly-i-cannot">62 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;But, I believe," I continue, "I know what true love is - or what it should be." <br /><br />"What should it be?" Tristan asks, his voice soft now. <br /><br />"It should be a friendship and truly knowing who a person is, knowing his flaws and hopes and strengths and fears, knowing all of it. And admiring and caring for - loving the person because of those things.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/158521-but-i-believe-i-continue-i-know-what-true-love">50 likes</a>
